	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Studio Ghibli</h1>
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		<div id="contentSub2"></div>
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>

		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Japanese animation studio</div>
<p>
<span style="font-size: small;"><span id="coordinates"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a>: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Studio_Ghibli&amp;params=35_42_11.5_N_139_31_44.9_E_type:landmark"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">35°42′11.5″N</span> <span class="longitude">139°31′44.9″E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">35.703194°N 139.529139°E</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">35.703194; 139.529139</span></span></span></a></span></span></span>
</p>

<p><b>Studio Ghibli Inc.</b><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a>: <span lang="ja">株式会社スタジオジブリ</span>, <a href="/wiki/Hepburn_romanization" title="Hepburn romanization">Hepburn</a>: <i lang="ja-Latn" title="Hepburn transliteration">Kabushiki-gaisha Sutajio Jiburi</i>)</span> is a <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">Japanese animation</a> film studio headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Koganei,_Tokyo" title="Koganei, Tokyo">Koganei, Tokyo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The studio is best known for its animated feature films, and has also produced several short films, television commercials, and one television film. It was founded on June 15, 1985 by directors <a href="/wiki/Hayao_Miyazaki" title="Hayao Miyazaki">Hayao Miyazaki</a> and <a href="/wiki/Isao_Takahata" title="Isao Takahata">Isao Takahata</a> and producer <a href="/wiki/Toshio_Suzuki_(producer)" title="Toshio Suzuki (producer)">Toshio Suzuki</a>, after the success of <a href="/wiki/Topcraft" title="Topcraft">Topcraft</a>'s anime film <i><a href="/wiki/Nausica%C3%A4_of_the_Valley_of_the_Wind_(film)" title="Nausicaä of the Valley of the Wind (film)">Nausicaä of the Valley of the Wind</a></i> (1984). Studio Ghibli has also collaborated with video game studios on the visual development of several video games.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Six of Studio Ghibli's films are among the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_anime_films" title="List of highest-grossing anime films">10 highest-grossing anime films</a> made in Japan, with <i><a href="/wiki/Spirited_Away" title="Spirited Away">Spirited Away</a></i> (2001) being the second highest, grossing over US$360 million worldwide. Many of their works have won the <a href="/wiki/Animage" title="Animage">Animage</a> Anime Grand Prix award, and four have won the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Academy_Prize_for_Animation_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="Japan Academy Prize for Animation of the Year">Japan Academy Prize for Animation of the Year</a>. Five of Studio Ghibli's films have received <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Award</a> nominations. <i><a href="/wiki/Spirited_Away" title="Spirited Away">Spirited Away</a></i> won the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Bear" title="Golden Bear">Golden Bear</a> in 2002 and the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Animated_Feature" title="Academy Award for Best Animated Feature">Academy Award for Best Animated Feature Film</a> in <a href="/wiki/75th_Academy_Awards" title="75th Academy Awards">2003</a>. Totoro, a character from <i><a href="/wiki/My_Neighbor_Totoro" title="My Neighbor Totoro">My Neighbor Totoro</a></i>, is the studio's mascot.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 3, 2014, Studio Ghibli temporarily halted production following the retirement of Miyazaki. In February 2017, Toshio Suzuki announced that Miyazaki had come out of retirement again to direct a new feature film, <i><a href="/wiki/How_Do_You_Live%3F_(film)" title="How Do You Live? (film)">How Do You Live?</a></i>, with Studio Ghibli.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Studio_Ghibli&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The name Ghibli was given by Hayao Miyazaki from the Italian noun <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ghibli" class="extiw" title="wikt:ghibli">ghibli</a></i>, based on the <a href="/wiki/Libyan_Arabic" title="Libyan Arabic">Libyan Arabic</a> name  for <a href="/wiki/Sirocco" title="Sirocco">hot desert wind</a> (قبلي, romanized: ghiblī), the idea being the studio would "blow a new wind through the anime industry".<sup id="cite_ref-name-ghibli_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-name-ghibli-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SG1_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SG1-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> It also refers to an Italian aircraft, the <a href="/wiki/Caproni_Ca.309" title="Caproni Ca.309">Caproni Ca.309</a>. Although the Italian word would be more accurately transliterated as <span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text">ギブリ</span> (<i>Giburi</i>), the Japanese name of the studio is <span lang="ja" title="Japanese language text">ジブリ</span> (<i>Jiburi</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Japanese" title="Help:IPA/Japanese">[dʑiꜜbɯɾi]</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ja-Ghibli.oga" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/32/Ja-Ghibli.oga" class="internal" title="Ja-Ghibli.oga">listen</a></span></span>)</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-name-ghibli_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-name-ghibli-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Studio_Ghibli&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tokuma_Shoten_era">Tokuma Shoten era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Studio_Ghibli&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Tokuma Shoten era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Toshio_Suzuki,_Howl%27s_Moving_Castle_premiere.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Toshio_Suzuki%2C_Howl%27s_Moving_Castle_premiere.jpg/300px-Toshio_Suzuki%2C_Howl%27s_Moving_Castle_premiere.jpg 2x" data-file-width="781" data-file-height="1016" /></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">Three of the four founders of Studio Ghibli. From top to bottom: <br /><a href="/wiki/Hayao_Miyazaki" title="Hayao Miyazaki">Hayao Miyazaki</a>, <br /><a href="/wiki/Isao_Takahata" title="Isao Takahata">Isao Takahata</a>, <br /><a href="/wiki/Toshio_Suzuki_(producer)" title="Toshio Suzuki (producer)">Toshio Suzuki</a></div></div></div></div>
<p>Founded on June 15, 1985, the studio was headed by directors Hayao Miyazaki and <a href="/wiki/Isao_Takahata" title="Isao Takahata">Isao Takahata</a> and producer <a href="/wiki/Toshio_Suzuki_(producer)" title="Toshio Suzuki (producer)">Toshio Suzuki</a>. Prior to the formation of the studio, Miyazaki and Takahata had already had long careers in Japanese film and television animation and had worked together on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Adventure_of_Horus,_Prince_of_the_Sun" title="The Great Adventure of Horus, Prince of the Sun">The Great Adventure of Horus, Prince of the Sun</a></i> in 1968 and the <i><a href="/wiki/Panda!_Go,_Panda!" title="Panda! Go, Panda!">Panda! Go, Panda!</a></i> films in 1972 and 1973, and in 1978, Suzuki became an editor at <a href="/wiki/Tokuma_Shoten" title="Tokuma Shoten">Tokuma Shoten</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Animage" title="Animage">Animage</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Manga" title="Manga">manga</a> magazine, where the first film he chose was <i>Horus</i>. A year after his phone call with Takahata and his first encounter with Miyazaki, both about <i>Horus</i>, he made a phone call about the first film Miyazaki ever directed: <i><a href="/wiki/The_Castle_of_Cagliostro" title="The Castle of Cagliostro">The Castle of Cagliostro</a></i>.
</p><p>The studio was founded after the success of the 1984 film <i><a href="/wiki/Nausica%C3%A4_of_the_Valley_of_the_Wind_(film)" title="Nausicaä of the Valley of the Wind (film)">Nausicaä of the Valley of the Wind</a></i>, written and directed by Miyazaki for <a href="/wiki/Topcraft" title="Topcraft">Topcraft</a> and distributed by <a href="/wiki/Toei_Company" title="Toei Company">Toei Company</a>. The origins of the film lie in the first two volumes of a <a href="/wiki/Nausica%C3%A4_of_the_Valley_of_the_Wind_(manga)" title="Nausicaä of the Valley of the Wind (manga)">serialized manga</a> written by Miyazaki for publication in <i>Animage</i> as a way of generating interest in an anime version.<sup id="cite_ref-SG1_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SG1-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Suzuki was part of the production team on the film and founded Studio Ghibli with Miyazaki, who also invited Takahata to join the new studio.
</p><p>The studio has mainly produced films by Miyazaki, with the second most prolific director being Takahata (most notably with <i><a href="/wiki/Grave_of_the_Fireflies" title="Grave of the Fireflies">Grave of the Fireflies</a></i>). Other directors who have worked with Studio Ghibli include <a href="/wiki/Yoshifumi_Kond%C5%8D" title="Yoshifumi Kondō">Yoshifumi Kondō</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hiroyuki_Morita" title="Hiroyuki Morita">Hiroyuki Morita</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gor%C5%8D_Miyazaki" title="Gorō Miyazaki">Gorō Miyazaki</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hiromasa_Yonebayashi" title="Hiromasa Yonebayashi">Hiromasa Yonebayashi</a>. Composer <a href="/wiki/Joe_Hisaishi" title="Joe Hisaishi">Joe Hisaishi</a> has provided the soundtracks for most of Miyazaki's Studio Ghibli films. In their book <i>Anime Classics Zettai!</i>, Brian Camp and Julie Davis made note of <a href="/wiki/Michiyo_Yasuda" title="Michiyo Yasuda">Michiyo Yasuda</a> as "a mainstay of Studio Ghibli’s extraordinary design and production team".<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> At one time the studio was based in <a href="/wiki/Kichij%C5%8Dji" title="Kichijōji">Kichijōji</a>, <a href="/wiki/Musashino,_Tokyo" title="Musashino, Tokyo">Musashino</a>, Tokyo.<sup id="cite_ref-FirefliesAnimerica11_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FirefliesAnimerica11-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 1996, <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">The Walt Disney Company</a> and Tokuma Shoten formed a partnership wherein <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Motion_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures">Walt Disney Studios</a> would be the sole international distributor for Tokuma Shoten's Studio Ghibli animated films.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Under this agreement, Disney also agreed to finance 10% of the studio's production costs.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Since then, all three aforementioned films by Miyazaki at Studio Ghibli that were previously dubbed by Streamline Pictures have been re-dubbed by Disney.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> On June 1, 1997, Tokuma Shoten Publishing consolidated its media operations by merging Studio Ghibli, Tokuma Shoten Intermedia software and Tokuma International under one location.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Over the years, there has been a close relationship between Studio Ghibli and the magazine <i>Animage</i>, which regularly runs exclusive articles on the studio and its members in a section titled "Ghibli Notes." Artwork from Ghibli's films and other works are frequently featured on the cover of the magazine. <a href="/wiki/Saeko_Himuro" title="Saeko Himuro">Saeko Himuro</a>'s novel <i>Umi ga Kikoeru</i> was serialised in the magazine and subsequently adapted into <i><a href="/wiki/Ocean_Waves_(film)" title="Ocean Waves (film)">Ocean Waves</a></i>, Studio Ghibli's only animated feature-length film created for television. It was directed by <a href="/wiki/Tomomi_Mochizuki" title="Tomomi Mochizuki">Tomomi Mochizuki</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nausicaa-faq_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nausicaa-faq-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2001, the <a href="/wiki/Ghibli_Museum" title="Ghibli Museum">Ghibli Museum</a> opened in <a href="/wiki/Mitaka,_Tokyo" title="Mitaka, Tokyo">Mitaka, Tokyo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> It contains exhibits based on Studio Ghibli films and shows animations, including a number of short Studio Ghibli films not available elsewhere.
</p><p>The studio is also known for its strict "no-edits" policy in licensing their films abroad due to <i>Nausicaä of the Valley of Wind</i> being <a href="/wiki/Editing_of_anime_in_American_distribution" class="mw-redirect" title="Editing of anime in American distribution">heavily edited</a> for the film's release in the United States as <i>Warriors of the Wind</i>. The "no cuts" policy was highlighted when <a href="/wiki/Miramax" title="Miramax">Miramax</a> co-chairman <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Weinstein" title="Harvey Weinstein">Harvey Weinstein</a> suggested editing <i><a href="/wiki/Princess_Mononoke" title="Princess Mononoke">Princess Mononoke</a></i> to make it more marketable. A Studio Ghibli producer is rumoured to have sent an authentic Japanese sword with a simple message: "No cuts".<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independent_era">Independent era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Studio_Ghibli&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Independent era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Between 1999 and 2005, Studio Ghibli was a subsidiary brand of Tokuma Shoten; however, that partnership ended in April 2005, when Studio Ghibli was spun off from Tokuma Shoten and was re-established as an independent company with relocated headquarters.
</p><p>On February 1, 2008, Toshio Suzuki stepped down from the position of Studio Ghibli president, which he had held since 2005, and Koji Hoshino (former president of Walt Disney Japan) took over. Suzuki said he wanted to improve films with his own hands as a producer, rather than demanding this from his employees. Suzuki decided to hand over the presidency to Hoshino because Hoshino has helped Studio Ghibli to sell its videos since 1996 and has also aided the release of the <i>Princess Mononoke</i> film in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Suzuki still serves on the company's board of directors.
</p><p>Two Studio Ghibli short films created for the <a href="/wiki/Ghibli_Museum" title="Ghibli Museum">Ghibli Museum</a> were shown at the Carnegie Hall Citywise Japan NYC Festival: "House Hunting" and "Mon Mon the Water Spider" were screened on March 26, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Takahata developed a project for release after Gorō Miyazaki's (director of <i><a href="/wiki/Tales_from_Earthsea_(film)" title="Tales from Earthsea (film)">Tales from Earthsea</a></i> and Hayao's son) <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tale_of_the_Princess_Kaguya" title="The Tale of the Princess Kaguya">The Tale of the Princess Kaguya</a></i> – an adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tale_of_the_Bamboo_Cutter" title="The Tale of the Bamboo Cutter">The Tale of the Bamboo Cutter</a></i>. The last film Hayao Miyazaki directed before retiring from feature films was <i><a href="/wiki/Kaze_Tachinu" class="mw-redirect" title="Kaze Tachinu">The Wind Rises</a></i> which is about the <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_A6M_Zero" title="Mitsubishi A6M Zero">Mitsubishi A6M Zero</a> and its founder.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On Sunday, September 1, 2013, Hayao Miyazaki held a press conference in Venice to confirm his retirement, saying: "I know I've said I would retire many times in the past. Many of you must think, 'Once again.' But this time I am quite serious."<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 31, 2014, it was announced that Gorō Miyazaki will direct his first anime television series, <i><a href="/wiki/Sanzoku_no_Musume_R%C5%8Dnya" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanzoku no Musume Rōnya">Sanzoku no Musume Rōnya</a></i>, an adaptation of <a href="/wiki/Astrid_Lindgren" title="Astrid Lindgren">Astrid Lindgren</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Ronia_the_Robber%27s_Daughter" class="mw-redirect" title="Ronia the Robber&#39;s Daughter">Ronia the Robber's Daughter</a></i> for <a href="/wiki/NHK" title="NHK">NHK</a>. The series is <a href="/wiki/Computer_animation" title="Computer animation">computer-animated</a>, produced by <a href="/wiki/Polygon_Pictures" title="Polygon Pictures">Polygon Pictures</a>, and co-produced by Studio Ghibli.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2014, <a href="/wiki/Toshio_Suzuki_(producer)" title="Toshio Suzuki (producer)">Toshio Suzuki</a> retired as producer and assumed the new position of general manager. Yoshiaki Nishimura replaced Suzuki in the producer role.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 3, 2014, Toshio Suzuki announced that Studio Ghibli would take a "brief pause" to re-evaluate and restructure in the wake of Miyazaki's retirement. He stated some concerns about where the company would go in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-variety_august_2014_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-variety_august_2014-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc-retire_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-retire-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> This led to speculation that Studio Ghibli will never produce another feature film again. On November 7, 2014, Miyazaki stated, "That was not my intention, though. All I did was announce that I would be retiring and not making any more features."<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Lead producer <a href="/wiki/Yoshiaki_Nishimura" title="Yoshiaki Nishimura">Yoshiaki Nishimura</a> among several other staffers from Ghibli, such as director <a href="/wiki/Hiromasa_Yonebayashi" title="Hiromasa Yonebayashi">Hiromasa Yonebayashi</a>, left to found <a href="/wiki/Studio_Ponoc" title="Studio Ponoc">Studio Ponoc</a> in April 2015, working on the film <i><a href="/wiki/Mary_and_the_Witch%27s_Flower" title="Mary and the Witch&#39;s Flower">Mary and the Witch's Flower</a></i>.
</p><p>The 2016 <a href="/wiki/Animation" title="Animation">animated</a> <a href="/wiki/Fantasy_film" title="Fantasy film">fantasy film</a> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Red_Turtle" title="The Red Turtle">The Red Turtle</a></i>, directed and co-written by Dutch-British animator <a href="/wiki/Micha%C3%ABl_Dudok_de_Wit" title="Michaël Dudok de Wit">Michaël Dudok de Wit</a> in his feature film debut, was a <a href="/wiki/International_co-production" class="mw-redirect" title="International co-production">co-production</a> between Studio Ghibli and <a href="/wiki/Wild_Bunch_(company)" title="Wild Bunch (company)">Wild Bunch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-red_turtle_production_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-red_turtle_production-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2017, Toshio Suzuki announced that Hayao Miyazaki had come out of retirement to direct a new feature film with Studio Ghibli.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On November 28, 2017, Koji Hoshino stepped down as president; he was replaced by Kiyofumi Nakajima (former Ghibli Museum director). Hoshino was then appointed as Chairman of Studio Ghibli.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2020, Toshio Suzuki confirmed that a new film from Gorō Miyazaki is in development at Studio Ghibli. On June 3, 2020, Studio Ghibli announced that the film would be an adaptation of the novel <i><a href="/wiki/Earwig_and_the_Witch" title="Earwig and the Witch">Earwig and the Witch</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Diana_Wynne_Jones" title="Diana Wynne Jones">Diana Wynne Jones</a>. The film was announced as the first full <a href="/wiki/3D_computer_graphics" title="3D computer graphics">3D CG</a> animated Ghibli film and slated for a television premiere on <a href="/wiki/NHK" title="NHK">NHK</a> in late 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-earwig-movie_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earwig-movie-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Distribution_rights">Distribution rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Studio_Ghibli&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Distribution rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatrical_and_home_media_rights">Theatrical and home media rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Studio_Ghibli&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Theatrical and home media rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Studio_Ghibli&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Japan, the company's films (and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Castle_of_Cagliostro" title="The Castle of Cagliostro">The Castle of Cagliostro</a></i> and all other <i><a href="/wiki/Lupin_the_Third" title="Lupin the Third">Lupin the Third</a></i> titles for movie theaters as well as <i><a href="/wiki/Mary_and_the_Witch%27s_Flower" title="Mary and the Witch&#39;s Flower">Mary and the Witch's Flower</a></i>) are distributed by <a href="/wiki/Toho" title="Toho">Toho</a> theatrically (except for <i><a href="/wiki/Castle_in_the_Sky" title="Castle in the Sky">Castle in the Sky</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Kiki%27s_Delivery_Service" title="Kiki&#39;s Delivery Service">Kiki's Delivery Service</a></i>, which were distributed by <a href="/wiki/Toei_Company" title="Toei Company">Toei Company</a> along with <i><a href="/wiki/Nausica%C3%A4_of_the_Valley_of_the_Wind_(film)" title="Nausicaä of the Valley of the Wind (film)">Nausicaä of the Valley of the Wind</a></i> (with Toei producing <i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Adventure_of_Horus,_Prince_of_the_Sun" title="The Great Adventure of Horus, Prince of the Sun">The Great Adventure of Horus, Prince of the Sun</a></i>), and <i><a href="/wiki/My_Neighbors_the_Yamadas" title="My Neighbors the Yamadas">My Neighbors the Yamadas</a></i>, which was distributed by <a href="/wiki/Shochiku" title="Shochiku">Shochiku</a>), and by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Home_Entertainment" title="Walt Disney Studios Home Entertainment">Walt Disney Studios Japan</a> on home media along with  <i><a href="/wiki/Nausica%C3%A4_of_the_Valley_of_the_Wind_(film)" title="Nausicaä of the Valley of the Wind (film)">Nausicaä of the Valley of the Wind</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Castle_of_Cagliostro" title="The Castle of Cagliostro">The Castle of Cagliostro</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Mary_and_the_Witch%27s_Flower" title="Mary and the Witch&#39;s Flower">Mary and the Witch's Flower</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-DisneyTokuma_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DisneyTokuma-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Before the Disney deal, Tokuma Shoten released Ghibli movies themselves through their "Animage Video" imprint, as well as all <a href="/wiki/Laserdisc" class="mw-redirect" title="Laserdisc">Laserdisc</a> releases of the movies, as the Disney deal didn't include that format until this summer in 1996.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Studio_Ghibli&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Manson International and Showmen, Inc. produced a 95-minute English-dubbed adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/Nausica%C3%A4_of_the_Valley_of_the_Wind_(film)" title="Nausicaä of the Valley of the Wind (film)">Nausicaä of the Valley of the Wind</a></i>, titled <i>Warriors of the Wind</i>, which was released theatrically in the United States by <a href="/wiki/New_World_Pictures" title="New World Pictures">New World Pictures</a> on June 13, 1985, followed by a VHS release in December 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In the late 1980s, <a href="/wiki/Vestron_Video" title="Vestron Video">Vestron Video</a> would re-release the film and First Independent Video would re-release it again in 1993, with another minute cut from the film. The voice actors and actresses were not credited and were not even informed of the film's plotline, and the film was <a href="/wiki/Editing_of_anime_in_American_distribution" class="mw-redirect" title="Editing of anime in American distribution">heavily edited</a> to market it as a children's <a href="/wiki/Action-adventure_film" class="mw-redirect" title="Action-adventure film">action-adventure film</a>, although the film received a PG rating just like Disney's later English dub.<sup id="cite_ref-FAQ_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAQ-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Consequently, part of the film's narrative meaning was lost: some of the environmentalist themes were diluted as was the main subplot of the Ohmu, altered to turn them into aggressive enemies. Most of the characters' names were changed, including the titular character who became Princess Zandra.<sup id="cite_ref-FAQ_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAQ-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The United States poster and VHS cover featured a cadre of male characters who are not in the film, riding the resurrected God Warrior—including a still-living Warrior shown briefly in a flashback.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Approximately 22 minutes of scenes were cut for the film's North American release. Dissatisfied with <i>Warriors of the Wind</i>, Miyazaki eventually adopted a strict "no-edits" clause for further foreign releases of the company's films.<sup id="cite_ref-FAQ_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAQ-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> <i>Warriors of the Wind</i> also prompted Miyazaki to allow translator <a href="/wiki/Toren_Smith" title="Toren Smith">Toren Smith</a> of <a href="/wiki/Studio_Proteus" title="Studio Proteus">Studio Proteus</a> to create an official, faithful translation of the <i>Nausicaä</i> manga for <a href="/wiki/Viz_Media" title="Viz Media">Viz Media</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the late 1980s, an English dubbed version of <i><a href="/wiki/Castle_in_the_Sky" title="Castle in the Sky">Castle in the Sky</a></i> was produced by Magnum Video Tape and Dubbing<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> for international <a href="/wiki/Japan_Airlines" title="Japan Airlines">Japan Airlines</a> flights at the request of Tokuma Shoten. The <i>Castle</i> dub was briefly screened in the United States by <a href="/wiki/Streamline_Pictures" title="Streamline Pictures">Streamline Pictures</a>. <a href="/wiki/Carl_Macek" title="Carl Macek">Carl Macek</a>, the head of Streamline, was disappointed with this dub, deeming it "adequate, but clumsy".<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Following this, Tokuma allowed Streamline to dub their future acquisitions <i><a href="/wiki/My_Neighbor_Totoro" title="My Neighbor Totoro">My Neighbor Totoro</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Kiki%27s_Delivery_Service" title="Kiki&#39;s Delivery Service">Kiki's Delivery Service</a></i>. In April 1993, <a href="/wiki/Troma_Entertainment" title="Troma Entertainment">Troma Films</a>, under their 50th St. Films banner, distributed the <i>Totoro</i> dub as a theatrical release, and the dub was later released onto VHS and eventually onto DVD by <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox_Home_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="20th Century Fox Home Entertainment">20th Century Fox Home Entertainment</a>. In the early 1990s, an English dubbed version of <i><a href="/wiki/Porco_Rosso" title="Porco Rosso">Porco Rosso</a></i> was produced by an unknown company, again for international Japan Airlines flights. The original dubs can be seen on the 1996 Ghibli ga Ippai Laserdisc set, and on the initial copies for the Japanese DVD releases of <i>Totoro</i>, <i>Laputa</i>, and <i>Porco</i>.
</p><p>In 1996, <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_(division)" title="Walt Disney Studios (division)">Walt Disney Studios</a> acquired worldwide distribution rights to the Studio Ghibli library, with Disney redubbing all previously dubbed films.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In addition, Walt Disney Studios Japan agreed to contribute 10% of the funding for all future releases, starting with <i><a href="/wiki/My_Neighbors_the_Yamadas" title="My Neighbors the Yamadas">My Neighbors the Yamadas</a></i>, in exchange for right of first refusal regarding international distribution.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Disney continues with this practice to this day, even extending it to the works of <a href="/wiki/Studio_Ponoc" title="Studio Ponoc">Studio Ponoc</a> and to co-productions like <i><a href="/wiki/The_Red_Turtle" title="The Red Turtle">The Red Turtle</a></i> in Japan. It was said to have taken four years for Disney and Studio Ghibli to reach a distribution deal. Originally, the Ghibli films were meant to headline a line of videos called <i>Animation Celebration</i>, highlighting critically acclaimed animated films from around the world. These plans never materialized in full, but the <i>Animation Celebration</i> logo can be seen on Disney's original VHS release of <i><a href="/wiki/Kiki%27s_Delivery_Service" title="Kiki&#39;s Delivery Service">Kiki's Delivery Service</a></i>. During Disney's tenure, the studio produced the English dubs and released 15 of Ghibli's films, plus <i><a href="/wiki/Nausica%C3%A4_of_the_Valley_of_the_Wind_(film)" title="Nausicaä of the Valley of the Wind (film)">Nausicaä of the Valley of the Wind</a></i> through the <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Home_Entertainment" title="Walt Disney Studios Home Entertainment">Buena Vista Home Video</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miramax" title="Miramax">Miramax</a> and <a href="/wiki/Touchstone_Pictures" title="Touchstone Pictures">Touchstone Pictures</a> banners.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2011, <a href="/wiki/GKIDS" title="GKIDS">GKIDS</a> acquired the North American theatrical distribution rights of the aforementioned Ghibli films, with <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Home_Entertainment" title="Walt Disney Studios Home Entertainment">Walt Disney Studios Home Entertainment</a> retaining the home video rights.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Afterwards, in 2013, GKIDS acquired the US and Canadian distribution rights to <i><a href="/wiki/From_Up_on_Poppy_Hill" title="From Up on Poppy Hill">From Up on Poppy Hill</a></i>. The film, which Disney passed on to GKIDS due to dealing with potential incest, marked the first time since 1996 that Disney handed a Studio Ghibli film off to another distributor. Afterwards, GKIDS would go on to distribute the films Disney found to be too mature or unmarketable for American audiences: <i><a href="/wiki/Only_Yesterday_(1991_film)" title="Only Yesterday (1991 film)">Only Yesterday</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Ocean_Waves" class="mw-redirect" title="Ocean Waves">Ocean Waves</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tale_of_the_Princess_Kaguya" title="The Tale of the Princess Kaguya">The Tale of the Princess Kaguya</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/When_Marnie_Was_There" title="When Marnie Was There">When Marnie Was There</a></i>. Finally, in July 2017, Disney relinquished its home video rights (with the exception of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wind_Rises" title="The Wind Rises">The Wind Rises</a>,</i> which remained with Disney until 2020 due to a distribution clause) to GKIDS, which currently handles all theatrical and home media distribution of Ghibli films in North America along with <i><a href="/wiki/Mary_and_the_Witch%27s_Flower" title="Mary and the Witch&#39;s Flower">Mary and the Witch's Flower</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Nonetheless, Disney still continues to handle select distribution in Japan (home media) and Taiwan.
</p><p>GKIDS' home media releases have been handled by multiple distributors. <a href="/wiki/Cinedigm" title="Cinedigm">Cinedigm</a> distributed the home media release of <i>Poppy Hill</i>, <a href="/wiki/Universal_Pictures_Home_Entertainment" title="Universal Pictures Home Entertainment">Universal Pictures Home Entertainment</a> distributed the home media releases of <i>Kaguya</i>, <i>Marnie</i>, <i>Mary</i>, <i>Yesterday</i> &amp; <i>Waves</i> and <a href="/wiki/Shout!_Factory" title="Shout! Factory">Shout! Factory</a> has distributed all subsequent releases thus far. The Studio Ghibli films owned by GKIDS were made available for digital purchases on most major services in the United States and Canada on December 17, 2019 through Shout! Factory.<sup id="cite_ref-verge-purchase_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-purchase-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internationally">Internationally</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Studio_Ghibli&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Internationally">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Outside Japan and North America since 2003, <a href="/wiki/Wild_Bunch_(company)" title="Wild Bunch (company)">Wild Bunch</a> has held international sales rights to Ghibli's film library.<sup id="cite_ref-WildBunch_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WildBunch-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The company sells distribution rights to separate distributors across the world, including <a href="/wiki/StudioCanal_UK" title="StudioCanal UK">StudioCanal UK</a> (United Kingdom and Ireland)<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">The Walt Disney Company</a> (Taiwan), <a href="/wiki/Wild_Bunch_(company)" title="Wild Bunch (company)">Wild Bunch</a> (France and Belgium), <a href="/wiki/Universum_Film" class="mw-redirect" title="Universum Film">Universum Film</a> (Germany), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lucky_Red&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lucky Red (page does not exist)">Lucky Red</a> (Italy) and <a href="/wiki/Madman_Entertainment" title="Madman Entertainment">Madman Entertainment</a> (Australia and New Zealand).
</p><p>Notably, <i><a href="/wiki/Arrietty" title="Arrietty">The Secret World of Arrietty</a></i> received a second dub exclusive to the United Kingdom, produced by StudioCanal, likely due to the film's origins being from <a href="/wiki/Mary_Norton_(author)" title="Mary Norton (author)">Mary Norton</a>'s British novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Borrowers" title="The Borrowers">The Borrowers</a></i>.
</p><p>Disney formerly held the international sales rights as well until Wild Bunch's purchase in 2003. Disney kept the French distribution rights to Ghibli’s library until September 2020, when it had expired and transitioned off to Wild Bunch.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Streaming_rights">Streaming rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Studio_Ghibli&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Streaming rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Prior to 2019, Studio Ghibli opted not to make its films available digitally, feeling that physical media and theatrical events like <a href="/wiki/GKIDS" title="GKIDS">GKIDS</a>' <a href="/wiki/GKIDS#Studio_Ghibli_Fest" title="GKIDS">Studio Ghibli Fest</a> would work more towards their goal of mindful care and curation for their films. Disney had previously lobbied for a streaming deal with Ghibli during their distribution tenure, but such attempts were never materialized.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The studio heads changed their minds after hearing a quote from American actor and director <a href="/wiki/Woody_Allen" title="Woody Allen">Woody Allen</a> about how there should be multiple outlets for feature films.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 17, 2019, <a href="/wiki/WarnerMedia" title="WarnerMedia">WarnerMedia</a>'s <a href="/wiki/HBO_Max" title="HBO Max">HBO Max</a> announced it had acquired exclusive streaming rights to Studio Ghibli's catalogue in the United States as part of a deal with <a href="/wiki/GKIDS" title="GKIDS">GKIDS</a>; these films were available when the service launched in May 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> On January 20, 2020, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a> acquired the exclusive streaming rights to this catalogue in all regions except for the United States (in which Netflix does have streaming rights to both <i><a href="/wiki/The_Castle_of_Cagliostro" title="The Castle of Cagliostro">The Castle of Cagliostro</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Mary_and_the_Witch%27s_Flower" title="Mary and the Witch&#39;s Flower">Mary and the Witch's Flower</a></i>), Canada and Japan, as part of a deal with Ghibli's international sales rights partner <a href="/wiki/Wild_Bunch_(company)" title="Wild Bunch (company)">Wild Bunch</a>. Seven of twenty-one films in the studio's catalogue were released on February 1, 2020, with the others following on March 1 and April 1.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Netflix then struck a separate deal with GKIDS for streaming rights in Canada which was announced on June 22, and came into effect on June 25 for most films.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Currently, no streaming rights deals have been announced for Studio Ghibli's home country of Japan.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grave_of_the_Fireflies"><i>Grave of the Fireflies</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Studio_Ghibli&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Grave of the Fireflies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Most of the above deals exclude <i><a href="/wiki/Grave_of_the_Fireflies" title="Grave of the Fireflies">Grave of the Fireflies</a></i>; unlike most of the other films, which were published by <a href="/wiki/Tokuma_Shoten" title="Tokuma Shoten">Tokuma Shoten</a>, <i>Grave of the Fireflies</i> was produced and is owned by <a href="/wiki/Shinchosha" title="Shinchosha">Shinchosha</a>, which also had published the short story it was based on, and as such, fell into different rights holdings.<sup id="cite_ref-verge-purchase_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-purchase-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Grave of the Fireflies</i> was released in Japan on <a href="/wiki/VHS" title="VHS">VHS</a> by Buena Vista Home Entertainment under the <i>Ghibli ga Ippai</i> Collection on August 7, 1998. On July 29, 2005, a <a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a> release was distributed through <a href="/wiki/Warner_Home_Video" class="mw-redirect" title="Warner Home Video">Warner Home Video</a>. Walt Disney Studios Japan released the complete collector's edition DVD on August 6, 2008. WDSJ released the film on <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" class="mw-redirect" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray</a> twice on July 18, 2012: one as a single release, and one in a two-film set with <i><a href="/wiki/My_Neighbor_Totoro" title="My Neighbor Totoro">My Neighbor Totoro</a></i>.
</p><p>It was released on VHS in North America by <a href="/wiki/Central_Park_Media" title="Central Park Media">Central Park Media</a> in a subtitled form on June 2, 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> They later released the film with an English dub on VHS on September 1, 1998 (the same day Disney released <i><a href="/wiki/Kiki%27s_Delivery_Service" title="Kiki&#39;s Delivery Service">Kiki's Delivery Service</a></i> in North America) and an all-Regions DVD (which also included the original Japanese with English subtitles) on October 7 the same year. It was later released on a two-disc DVD set (which once again included both the English dub and the original Japanese with English subtitles as well as the film's storyboards with the second disc containing more extensive Bonus Features) on October 8, 2002. It was released by Central Park Media one last time on December 7, 2004. Following the May 2009 bankruptcy and liquidation of Central Park Media,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/A.D._Vision#ADV_Films" title="A.D. Vision">ADV Films</a> acquired the rights and re-released it on DVD on July 7, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Following the September 1, 2009 shutdown and re-branding of ADV,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> their successor, <a href="/wiki/Sentai_Filmworks" title="Sentai Filmworks">Sentai Filmworks</a>, rescued the film and released a remastered DVD on March 6, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Martin_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martin-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray" title="Blu-ray">Blu-ray</a> edition was released on November 20, 2012, featuring an all-new English dub produced by <a href="/wiki/Seraphim_Digital" title="Seraphim Digital">Seraphim Digital</a>, along with a digital release that same year.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/StudioCanal" title="StudioCanal">StudioCanal</a> released a Blu-ray in the United Kingdom on July 1, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Madman_Entertainment" title="Madman Entertainment">Madman Entertainment</a> released the film in Australia and New Zealand.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Works">Works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Studio_Ghibli&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Studio_Ghibli_works" title="List of Studio Ghibli works">List of Studio Ghibli works</a></div>
<p>While not technically Studio Ghibli films, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Adventure_of_Horus,_Prince_of_the_Sun" title="The Great Adventure of Horus, Prince of the Sun">The Great Adventure of Horus, Prince of the Sun</a></i> (1968), <i><a href="/wiki/Panda!_Go_Panda!" class="mw-redirect" title="Panda! Go Panda!">Panda! Go Panda!</a></i> (1972), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Castle_of_Cagliostro" title="The Castle of Cagliostro">The Castle of Cagliostro</a></i> (1979), <i><a href="/wiki/Jarinko_Chie" title="Jarinko Chie">Jarinko Chie</a></i> (1981), <i><a href="/wiki/Gauche_the_Cellist" title="Gauche the Cellist">Gauche the Cellist</a></i> (1982), <i><a href="/wiki/Nausica%C3%A4_of_the_Valley_of_the_Wind_(film)" title="Nausicaä of the Valley of the Wind (film)">Nausicaä of the Valley of the Wind</a></i> (1984), <i><a href="/wiki/Mary_and_the_Witch%27s_Flower" title="Mary and the Witch&#39;s Flower">Mary and the Witch's Flower</a></i> (2017), and <i><a href="/wiki/Modest_Heroes" title="Modest Heroes">Modest Heroes</a></i> (2018) are sometimes grouped together with the Studio Ghibli library (particularly with the <i>Ghibli ga Ippai</i> home video collection released by Walt Disney Studios Japan) due to their ties to the studio.
</p><p><i>Horus</i> and <i>Cagliostro</i> were the feature-length directorial debuts of Isao Takahata and Hayao Miyazaki respectively, and were produced by <a href="/wiki/Toei_Animation" title="Toei Animation">Toei Animation</a> and <a href="/wiki/TMS_Entertainment" title="TMS Entertainment">TMS Entertainment</a> years before the founding of Studio Ghibli.
</p><p><i>Nausicaä</i> was directed by Miyazaki at <a href="/wiki/Topcraft" title="Topcraft">Topcraft</a>, a studio which Miyazaki, Takahata and <a href="/wiki/Toshio_Suzuki_(producer)" title="Toshio Suzuki (producer)">Toshio Suzuki</a> later purchased and renamed Studio Ghibli. As a result, the film has often been rereleased and marketed as a Studio Ghibli movie.
</p><p><i>The Red Turtle</i> was a collaborative effort by Studio Ghibli with Dutch animator <a href="/wiki/Micha%C3%ABl_Dudok_de_Wit" title="Michaël Dudok de Wit">Michaël Dudok de Wit</a> and was branded as a Studio Ghibli release internationally. It was distributed by <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Classics" title="Sony Pictures Classics">Sony Pictures Classics</a> in North and Latin America.
</p><p><i>Mary and the Witch's Flower</i> and <i>Modest Heroes</i> were produced by <a href="/wiki/Studio_Ponoc" title="Studio Ponoc">Studio Ponoc</a>, a company founded by Studio Ghibli veterans <a href="/wiki/Yoshiaki_Nishimura" title="Yoshiaki Nishimura">Yoshiaki Nishimura</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hiromasa_Yonebayashi" title="Hiromasa Yonebayashi">Hiromasa Yonebayashi</a> following the 2014 restructuring of Ghibli.
</p><p>For the purposes of the list below, only films fully produced and released by Studio Ghibli are listed. Other Studio Ghibli productions are listed <a href="/wiki/List_of_Studio_Ghibli_works" title="List of Studio Ghibli works">here.</a>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Feature_films">Feature films</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Studio_Ghibli&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Feature films">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_animators_and_character_designers">Notable animators and character designers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Studio_Ghibli&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Notable animators and character designers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Masashi_Ando" title="Masashi Ando">Masashi Ando</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Paranoia_Agent" title="Paranoia Agent">Paranoia Agent</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Paprika_(2006_film)" title="Paprika (2006 film)">Paprika</a></i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Makiko_Futaki" title="Makiko Futaki">Makiko Futaki</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Akira_(1988_film)" title="Akira (1988 film)">Akira</a></i>, <i>Angel's Egg</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Katsuya_Kond%C5%8D" title="Katsuya Kondō">Katsuya Kondō</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Kiki%27s_Delivery_Service" title="Kiki&#39;s Delivery Service">Kiki's Delivery Service</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Howl%27s_Moving_Castle_(film)" title="Howl&#39;s Moving Castle (film)">Howl's Moving Castle</a></i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kitar%C5%8D_K%C5%8Dsaka" title="Kitarō Kōsaka">Kitarō Kōsaka</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Monster_(manga)" title="Monster (manga)">Monster</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Master_Keaton" title="Master Keaton">Master Keaton</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Nasu_(manga)" title="Nasu (manga)">Nasu</a></i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kazuo_Oga" title="Kazuo Oga">Kazuo Oga</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Night_of_Taneyamagahara" title="The Night of Taneyamagahara">The Night of Taneyamagahara</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/My_Neighbor_Totoro" title="My Neighbor Totoro">My Neighbor Totoro</a></i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kenichi_Yoshida_(animator)" title="Kenichi Yoshida (animator)">Kenichi Yoshida</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Overman_King_Gainer" title="Overman King Gainer">Overman King Gainer</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Eureka_Seven" title="Eureka Seven">Eureka Seven</a></i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Akihiko_Yamashita" title="Akihiko Yamashita">Akihiko Yamashita</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Tide-Line_Blue" title="Tide-Line Blue">Tide-Line Blue</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Princess_Nine" title="Princess Nine">Princess Nine</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Strange_Dawn" title="Strange Dawn">Strange Dawn</a></i>, and <i>Relic Armor Legacium</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hideaki_Anno" title="Hideaki Anno">Hideaki Anno</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Nausica%C3%A4_of_the_Valley_of_the_Wind_(film)" title="Nausicaä of the Valley of the Wind (film)">Nausicaä of the Valley of the Wind</a></i>)</li></ul>

<li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite id="CITEREFMacek" class="citation news cs1">Macek, Carl. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.animenewsnetwork.com/anncast/2014-01-09">"ANN Cast Episode 23"</a>. <i>Anime News Network</i>. And I told the people at Tokuma Shoten that I thought the dubbing was marginal on <i>Laputa</i> and I thought that it could be a better product if they had a better dubbing... To me, there's a certain element of class that you can bring to a project. <i>Laputa</i> is a very classy film, so it required a classy dub and the dub given to that particular film was adequate but clumsy. I didn't like it all... It's not something that I appreciated intellectually as well as aesthetically.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Anime+News+Network&amp;rft.atitle=ANN+Cast+Episode+23&amp;rft.aulast=Macek&amp;rft.aufirst=Carl&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.animenewsnetwork.com%2Fanncast%2F2014-01-09&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AStudio+Ghibli" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r982806391"/></span>
